  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a5b38244-cc2b-429a-b47c-94602231dc16'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer17106725728501505117">Several months have passed, and Roland’s two new tet-mates have become proficient gunslingers.   <span id="freeText17106725728501505117" style="display:none">Several months have passed, and Roland’s two new tet-mates have become proficient gunslingers. Eddie Dean has given up heroin, and Odetta’s two selves have joined, becoming the stronger and more balanced personality of Susannah Dean. But while battling The Pusher in 1977 New York, Roland altered ka by saving the life of Jake Chambers, a boy who—in Roland’s where and when—has already died. Now Roland and Jake exist in different worlds, but they are joined by the same madness: the paradox of double memories. Roland, Susannah, and Eddie must draw Jake into Mid-World then follow the Path of the Beam all the way to the Dark Tower. But nothing is easy in Mid-World. Along the way our tet stumbles into the ruined city of Lud, and are caught between the warring gangs of the Pubes and the Grays. The only way out of Lud is to wake Blaine the Mono, an insane train that has a passion for riddling, and for suicidal journeys.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17106725728501505117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_6595548" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6595548" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6595548?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/9745861-the-waste-lands">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=uncle-stevie">uncle-stevie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=dark-tower">dark-tower</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=western">western</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=alt-universes">alt-universes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2011-r">2011-r</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6595548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4029698209021792322">This book contains the biggest lie a writer ever told me. It‘s in the Author‘s Note at the end:<br/><br/><i>The fourth volume in the tale of the Dark Tower should appear - always assuming the continuation of Constant Writer’s life and Constant Reader’s interest - in the not-too-distant-future.</i><br/><br/>It took six years for the next book to come out. <br/><br/>Six. Goddamn. Years.<br/><br/>Six years may not seem too bad to fans of authors who only release a book every decade or so, but there’s a couple of factors that made this false sta</span>
  <span id="freeText4029698209021792322" style="display:none">This book contains the biggest lie a writer ever told me. It‘s in the Author‘s Note at the end:<br /><br /><i>The fourth volume in the tale of the Dark Tower should appear - always assuming the continuation of Constant Writer’s life and Constant Reader’s interest - in the not-too-distant-future.</i><br /><br />It took six years for the next book to come out. <br /><br />Six. Goddamn. Years.<br /><br />Six years may not seem too bad to fans of authors who only release a book every decade or so, but there’s a couple of factors that made this false statement particularly bitter. <i>The Waste Lands</i> ends on a nail biting cliffhanger. I literally yelled aloud in frustration the first time I read this back in 1991 and realized that I’d have to wait for the next book to learn the fate of Roland and his friends. <br /><br />Still, after some reflection it didn’t seem that bad. The next volume would appear ‘in the not-too-distant-future’, right? Besides this was Stephen King, the writer who churned out 1000 page books like McDonald’s makes Big Macs. No big deal. I’d be reading it by ‘92. 1993 at the latest.<br /><br />Five goddamn years later, and I’d gone from Stephen King and Dark Tower fan to the kind of crazed fury usually reserved for jilted lovers. It didn’t help that King was cranking out big fat books including some utter shit like <i>Insomnia</i> and <i>Rose Madder</i>. Yet no fourth Dark Tower book, and every now and then I’d reread the first three volumes and dream of the day when I’d finally learn what happened next.<br /><br />The odd thing is that it still kind of pisses me off even now that the series is finished. I get that same sense of frustration when I read this remembering the six goddamn years between books while seeing all kinds of other King novels come out. It’s too bad because this was my favorite of the first three books until frustration turned it into an irritating loose end.<br /><br />And I’ll confess something that makes me a small, petty person. Deep down in my shriveled black soul, I’m resentful and jealous of anyone who reads the series now or who started reading it when the last three books were coming out like clockwork at the end. They didn’t suffer like the ones who read this and waited six years. Then read the fourth one and waited <b>SIX MORE GODDAMN YEARS FOR THE FIFTH ONE. YEAH, THAT’S RIGHT! BETWEEN 1991 AND 2003 STEPHEN FUCKING KING, ONE-OF-THE-MOST-PROFILIC-WRITERS-I’VE-EVER-READ, MANAGED TO WRITE JUST ONE GODDAMN DARK TOWER BOOK AND IF THAT MINIVAN HADN’T VERY NEARLY KILLED HIS PROCRASTINATING ASS, I’D PROBABLY STILL BE WAITING!!</b><br /><br /><i>*ahem*</i> Excuse me. I’ve still got a few unresolved issues with old Steve about this series.<br /><br />And what about the story in this book? Roland is training Eddie and Susannah to be gunslingers, but he’s going crazy from a paradox he created in the last book by time hopping to our world and changing an event that altered his own timeline. They also find a creepy old decayed city filled with a murderous mob and have to deal with a monorail that is criminally insane.<br /><br />It’s terrific, but I think the waiting drove me a little mad. And now King has been making noises about possibly doing another book that would fill some of the <b>SIX GODDAMN YEAR GAP</b> between #4 and #5. You’ll pardon me if I don’t hold my breath.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4029698209021792322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2063995625" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2063995625" />
    <a title="Luca Ambrosino" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53478239-luca-ambrosino"><img alt="Luca Ambrosino" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523134271p2/53478239.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2063995625?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luca Ambrosino" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luca Ambrosino" href="/user/show/53478239-luca-ambrosino">Luca Ambrosino</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788868363680" href="/book/show/35695741-terre-desolate">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2063995625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13903606931680698706">English (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28335914.The_Waste_Lands__The_Dark_Tower__3_' title='The Waste Lands (The Dark Tower #3) by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Waste Lands</a>) / Italiano<br/><br/><p>Happiness while watching the drawing of the metal plate found on the just killed bear, happiness that I feel for the unpredictable and the inexplicable. My personal journey into the world of <i>"The Dark Tower"</i> goes on, together with the gunslinger, Roland, escorted by Eddie and Susannah, the two tale gunners recruited in the previous chapter, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5094.The_Drawing_of_the_Three__The_Dark_Tower___2_' title='The Drawing of the Three (The Dark Tower, #2) by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Drawing of the Three</a>. However, there is still somebody to recruit for the company to be complete...</p><p>In the author's no</p></span>
  <span id="freeText13903606931680698706" style="display:none">English (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28335914.The_Waste_Lands__The_Dark_Tower__3_" title="The Waste Lands (The Dark Tower #3) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Waste Lands</a>) / Italiano<br><br><p>Happiness while watching the drawing of the metal plate found on the just killed bear, happiness that I feel for the unpredictable and the inexplicable. My personal journey into the world of <i>"The Dark Tower"</i> goes on, together with the gunslinger, Roland, escorted by Eddie and Susannah, the two tale gunners recruited in the previous chapter, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5094.The_Drawing_of_the_Three__The_Dark_Tower___2_" title="The Drawing of the Three (The Dark Tower, #2) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Drawing of the Three</a>. However, there is still somebody to recruit for the company to be complete...</p><p>In the author's note at the end of the book, King predicts that some readers will probably be disappointed by the unanswered questions that this novel leaves. But actually, the philosophy of unanswered questions was the winning strategy of a lot of narrative or television series, such as the famous TV show <i>"LOST"</i> (which I loved), and I'm going to go out on a limb here expecting that it will be the winning strategy of <i>"The Dark Tower"</i> too.</p><p>Alright, cut the chatter. As Blaine the mono says:</p><blockquote>"... let the contest begin."</blockquote><p>Vote: 7,5</p><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504168285i/23730168._SX540_.jpg" width="420" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><p>Felicità mentre osservo il disegno della targa metallica rinvenuta sull'orso appena ucciso, felicità di <i>LOSTiana</i> memoria che provo per l'ignoto e l'inspiegabile. Continua il mio viaggio personale nel mondo de <i>"La Torre Nera"</i>, e continua il cammino di Roland, accompagnato da Eddie e Susannah, i due compagni di ventura reclutati nel precedente capitolo <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9553274.La_Chiamata_dei_Tre__La_Torre_Nera___2_" title="La Chiamata dei Tre (La Torre Nera, #2) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">La chiamata dei tre</a>. Tuttavia manca ancora qualcuno da reclutare affinchè la compagnia possa dirsi completa...</p><p>Nella nota dell'autore a fine libro, King prevede che probabilmente alcuni lettori saranno delusi dal fatto che <i>Terre Desolate</i> lascia tanti quesiti irrisolti. Beh, quella dei quesiti irrisolti è stata la filosofia vincente di tante serie narrative o televisive, come la serie cult <i>"LOST"</i>, della quale sono stato un fan sfegatato, e mi sbilancio con ottimismo prevedendo che sarà la filosofia vincente anche de <i>"La Torre Nera"</i>.</p><p>Okay, bando alle ciance. E come direbbe Blaine il Mono:</p><blockquote>"...che abbia inizio la gara."</blockquote><p>Voto: 7,5</p></span>

<div id="review_2320519363" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2320519363" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2320519363?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=king-stephen">king-stephen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320519363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9311163082252605191">Rolands´ DIY tutorials, worsening causality problems, time paradoxes, and the first real, longer encounters with paranormal activities and monsters let one dive deeper into the marvelous madness.<br/><br/>Just as in the second part, The drawing of the three, King is using some elements of the real, alternative world, although the main parts play in fantasy terror land, where the lovely hero´s journey of mentally ill, severely injured and mutilated, and fresh cold turkeyed protagonists can continue.<br/><br/>This on</span>
  <span id="freeText9311163082252605191" style="display:none">Rolands´ DIY tutorials, worsening causality problems, time paradoxes, and the first real, longer encounters with paranormal activities and monsters let one dive deeper into the marvelous madness.<br /><br />Just as in the second part, The drawing of the three, King is using some elements of the real, alternative world, although the main parts play in fantasy terror land, where the lovely hero´s journey of mentally ill, severely injured and mutilated, and fresh cold turkeyed protagonists can continue.<br /><br />This one is similar to the first part of the series, a good oldfashioned tour de force, while the second and fourth part are more personal, character focused works with fewer settings and action. I don´t know if King intended to switch the narrative styles between the parts or if it was a coincidence, but slowing down for a novel between, to focus on character development to accelerate in the next book, seems reasonable, although it sparked debates of fans about the uncertainty what the next part may bring. Depending on what style one prefers, the agreeableness can vary, a bit of fandom frenzy included. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The huge cyborg beast Shardik  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> lets me think about something I possibly could once have already mentioned in another review, either talking about King or Pratchett, how it would have been if they would have discovered the endless horrible and funny elements, tropes, and potentials of Sci-Fi for their works. That wouldn´t just have been an extra icing on the cake, it could have given it all so much more potential for perversion, cruelty, and inhumanity that it could have blown readers' minds even more. A wonderful imagination that my beloved genre Sci-Fi could have had Pratchetts´ humor or Kings´ terror next to the worldbuilding and often unique ideas some Sci-Fi authors succeeded in establishing.<br /><br />Manipulating reality can lead to funny results and King uses it to mind penetrate a younger version of one of the characters and possibly integrating himself, meanwhile sober, as the cocaine addicted father.<br /><br />Did I mention the explicit succubus incubus style sex scene <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ with extreme plot relevant consequences, because it´s not artificial insemination or in vitro fertilization that fulfills the wish for a child in Kings´ universe, it´s dark magic demon breeding monster hentai mutation by rape  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, because if all other arguments didn´t convince you to read it, this certainly will. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Who is my cute, world eating, monster baby, gugu?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The Tick Tock Man is in the house too, awaiting you in a kind of steampunky dystopian setting and wait until you can cuddle your first billy- bumbler, how cute, exactly what one needs in wastelands <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ filled with mutants and mad AIs <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> to calm down a bit and get some tenderness.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/TheWastelands">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9311163082252605191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1543341690" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1543341690" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1543341690?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/94767.The_Waste_Lands">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48328025-megs-bookrack?shelf=stephen-king-read">stephen-king-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1543341690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3727593739851977525">Let's cut right to the chase, shall we? <br/><br/><i>The Waste Lands</i> <b>blew my mind</b>. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460585561ra/18762460.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The riddles, Blaine the Mono, I mean, who comes up with this stuff?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543772919ra/26678294.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>The King</b>, that's who. <br/><br/>Stephen. FRICKING. King.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524413271ra/25416441.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>What more can I say besides the fact that I loved this with my whole heart and soul?!<br/><br/>As you know, if you are reading this, this is the third book in King's epic Dark Tower series. This book knocked <i>The Drawing of Three</i> out of the top spot for me. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493981891ra/22672296.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It was that good! As the series continues to build, it's hard not to b</span>
  <span id="freeText3727593739851977525" style="display:none">Let's cut right to the chase, shall we? <br><br><i>The Waste Lands</i> <b>blew my mind</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460585561ra/18762460.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The riddles, Blaine the Mono, I mean, who comes up with this stuff?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543772919ra/26678294.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The King</b>, that's who. <br><br>Stephen. FRICKING. King.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524413271ra/25416441.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What more can I say besides the fact that I loved this with my whole heart and soul?!<br><br>As you know, if you are reading this, this is the third book in King's epic Dark Tower series. This book knocked <i>The Drawing of Three</i> out of the top spot for me. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493981891ra/22672296.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It was that good! As the series continues to build, it's hard not to be overwhelmed by the complexity of it all. Even with this in mind however, it's such an enjoyable story. It just seems to work.<br><br>The most compelling element of this for me was the resurgence of my favorite character!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463647159ra/19141527.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There is really nothing else I can say about this that would be any more creative, or insightful, than what countless others have no doubt written in their reviews. <br><br>For me, one thing I always think when reading a book from this series is how absolutely <u>EPIC</u> it is. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496627406ra/22935481.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The detail, the atmosphere, the artfully drawn characters, it is truly astounding to me that all of this, <u>ALL OF THIS</u>, came out of one man's brain! <br><br>I look forward to seeing this series out to its conclusion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3727593739851977525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4006380614833322247">The Waste Lands (The Dark Tower, #3), Stephen King<br/>The Waste Lands (subtitled "Redemption") is a fantasy novel by American writer Stephen King, the third book of The Dark Tower series. The original limited edition hardcover featuring full-color illustrations by Ned Dameron was published in 1991 by Grant. Roland, Susannah, a</span>
  <span id="freeText4006380614833322247" style="display:none">The Waste Lands (The Dark Tower, #3), Stephen King<br />The Waste Lands (subtitled "Redemption") is a fantasy novel by American writer Stephen King, the third book of The Dark Tower series. The original limited edition hardcover featuring full-color illustrations by Ned Dameron was published in 1991 by Grant. The book was reissued in 2003 to coincide with the publication of The Dark Tower V: Wolves of the Calla. The story begins five weeks after the end of The Drawing of the Three. Roland, Susannah, and Eddie have moved east from the shore of the Western Sea, and into the woods of Out-World. After an encounter with a gigantic cyborg bear named Shardik, they discover one of the six mystical Beams that hold the world together. The three gunslingers follow the Path of the Beam inland to Mid-World. Roland now reveals to his ka-tet (group of people bound together by fate/destiny) that his mind has become divided and is slowly losing his sanity. Roland remembers meeting Jake Chambers in the way station and letting him fall to his death in the mountains (as depicted in The Dark Tower: The Gunslinger). However, he also remembers passing through the desert alone and never meeting Jake. It is soon discovered that when Roland saved Jake from being killed by Jack Mort in 1977 (in The Drawing of the Three), he inadvertently created a paradox; Jake did not die and thus did not appear in Mid-World and travel with Roland. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و هفتم ماه دسامبر سال 2014 میلادی<br />کتاب سوم از هفتگانه برج تاریک<br />عنوان: سرزمین متروک؛ اثر: استیون کینگ؛ برگردان: ندا شادنظر؛ مشخصات نشر: تهران، افراز، 1392، در 462 ص، شابک: 9789642433537؛ کتاب سوم از هفتگانه برج تاریک؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی سده 20 م<br /><br />کتاب «سرزمین متروک»، سومین رمان، از مجموعه ی داستانی «برج تاریک»، نوشته ی استیون کینگ، است. در این داستان، رولاند، آخرین هفت تیرکش، بیشتر از هر زمان دیگری، به برج تاریک رویاها، و کابوسهایش، نزدیک شده است. او از صحرایی نفرین شده در دنیای مهیب و ترسناکی میگذرد، که به گونه ای، تصویری از همین دنیای ما انسانهاست. دو شخصیت با نامهای: «ادی دین»، و «سوسانا» نیز، رولاند را، در این دنیا همراهی میکنند. خطرهای تازه ای، رولاند و همراهان اندکش را، در شهر ویرانه ی «لود»، و سرزمینهای متروک دور و اطراف، تهدید میکنند. رولاند با پیشروی داستان، به تدریج درمییابد، که چه کسی، یا چه چیزی، در پشت پرده، کنترل رخدادها را به دست دارد. او مجبور است، برای بقا با خیل عظیمی از دشمنان: انسان، و غیرانسان، رودررو شود. ا. شربیانی</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14801059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2530170929187087739">After the events of the Drawing of the Three, Roland the Gunslinger has two people from our world along side him in his quest for the Dark Tower. However, he's also going mad because of a strange double set of memories in his head, memories of a boy he crossed the desert with...<br/><br/>The Waste Lands is probably my favorite Dark Tower book and epitomizes what I like about the series. It's got the lost technology, lots of action, more bits about Roland's world, and makes Roland's ka-tet complete. The st</span>
  <span id="freeText2530170929187087739" style="display:none">After the events of the Drawing of the Three, Roland the Gunslinger has two people from our world along side him in his quest for the Dark Tower. However, he's also going mad because of a strange double set of memories in his head, memories of a boy he crossed the desert with...<br /><br />The Waste Lands is probably my favorite Dark Tower book and epitomizes what I like about the series. It's got the lost technology, lots of action, more bits about Roland's world, and makes Roland's ka-tet complete. The story of Jake in New York was well done. I even liked Oy the Billy-Bumbler. All the stuff that goes down in Lud had me dying to read the next book in the series. The ending would have made me furious had I been reading the Dark Tower books as they were published.<br /><br /><b>Notes from the 2011 re-read:</b><br />The Waste Lands drives home the notion that Roland's world is coming apart at the seams. It also gives us hints about what Roland was like before the world moved on, hints that will be further explored in Wizard and Glass.<br /><br />Even though I knew the whole deal with the key, this being my fifth or sixth read, it was still a tense moment when the key didn't turn and the creature was loose in the haunted mansion in New York. I felt a single man tear threaten to roll down my cheek when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Roland and Jake <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> were reunited.<br /><br />I also liked the Robert Howard reference, this being the first re-read since I read all the Howard Conan stuff.<br /><br />As I said after my re-read of The Gunslinger, it's a testament to Stephen King's skill that I was still a little worried about Jake in Lud, even though I've read the book a few times before.<br /><br />Blaine is a pain and that's the truth.<br /><br /><b>Notes from the 2014 re-read:</b><br />I always forget about Roland having to deal with the time paradox he created. Roland and Jake both going mad because of it was really well done and pretty believable. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Are the robots at the portal symbolic of the ultimately circular nature of Roland's quest? Did King know how the story would end way back when he wrote The Wastelands? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Every damn time, King still hooks me with the Jake situations in the mansion and in Lud. That's why he's a bajillionaire, I guess.<br /><br />If I couldn't have dogs, I'd take a billy-bumbler.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2530170929187087739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13158339071667056171">“Ka was like a wheel, its one purpose to turn, and in the end it always came back to the place where it had started.”<br/><br/>The third book in the Dark Tower series finds Roland and his ka-tet following the Path of the Beam towards the tower. Along the way they’ll pick up two new members...<br/><br/>I was contemplating writing this review as an Ode to Oy, but words can’t even express how much I love that little billy-bumbler; he is the CUTEST. A particular highlight for me is when he calls Gasher “asshole” - SASS</span>
  <span id="freeText13158339071667056171" style="display:none">“Ka was like a wheel, its one purpose to turn, and in the end it always came back to the place where it had started.”<br /><br />The third book in the Dark Tower series finds Roland and his ka-tet following the Path of the Beam towards the tower. Along the way they’ll pick up two new members...<br /><br />I was contemplating writing this review as an Ode to Oy, but words can’t even express how much I love that little billy-bumbler; he is the CUTEST. A particular highlight for me is when he calls Gasher “asshole” - SASSY OY!<br /><br />I also have a revelation that may shake you all to your cores... having previously ranted and raved about how Blaine did my head in, I actually LIKED Blaine the Mono this time around. Now, the riddles I can still do without... but I found Blaine to be highly entertaining. Memory is a funny thing, isn’t it?! He was completely different in my head!<br /><br />The house on Dutch Hill - how STRESSFUL is that part, the bleakness of Lud, the people in River Crossing, that huge freakin’ bear, MEETING OY..... this book has so much fucking awesomeness packed into it that I don’t know where to begin and I can’t fit it all in here in detail, so I’ll just say it was INCREDIBLE.<br /><br />This reread is completely challenging all my prior thoughts and feelings on certain books in the series. Now, I would rank The Waste Lands as the best in the series so far - whereas before, it was down near the bottom for me (but still excellent, I do love all the books!) This one has gained an entire star following my reread!<br /><br />I honestly hate reviewing these books because it’s just word vomit. I JUST LOVE THIS SERIES SO MUCH. 5 glittering shiny stars!!</span>

    <a title="Adina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22189348-adina"><img alt="Adina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531917330p2/22189348.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22189348-adina?shelf=horror">horror</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2003447933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17327537682466823992">4.5*<br/><br/>I almost, almost, gave 5 stars to this one. I consider this volume to be the best out of the three that I’ve read so far. If the book had stopped midway it would have got the maximum recognition from me, no doubt. I love and hate King’s way of writing too much. He managed to keep me at the edge of my seat for 100 pages, hungry for more, promising my undying love and then, after the climax (the forth drawing), he slightly bores me for the next 100. Maybe the plot got too intense and he though</span>
  <span id="freeText17327537682466823992" style="display:none">4.5*<br /><br />I almost, almost, gave 5 stars to this one. I consider this volume to be the best out of the three that I’ve read so far. If the book had stopped midway it would have got the maximum recognition from me, no doubt. I love and hate King’s way of writing too much. He managed to keep me at the edge of my seat for 100 pages, hungry for more, promising my undying love and then, after the climax (the forth drawing), he slightly bores me for the next 100. Maybe the plot got too intense and he thought we needed a cool down but still, my serotonin levels dropped too much. <br /><br />The best part of the novel for me was the drawing of the 4th member of the Ka-tet after an adrenaline pumping sequence of evince in both worlds. I was enthralled by the changing of perspective from one world to another. The tension of those moments was King at his best. Even breathing was a nuisance as I feverishly turned page after page in order to see what happens next. <br /><br />The Waste Lands is the first in the series to finish with a cliffhanger but I won’t be rushing to start the next one as I do not want to overdose on King and lose interest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17327537682466823992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2490199062" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2490199062" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2490199062?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2490199062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6716594619655867632">“April is the cruellest month”<br/><br/>Stephen King’s ambitious and challenging Dark Tower series continues with the third novel, The Waste Lands, first published in 1991.<br/><br/>I am reading this series very slowly. I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43615.The_Gunslinger__The_Dark_Tower___1_' title='The Gunslinger (The Dark Tower, #1) by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Gunslinger</a> in 2012, not really sure what I had read and why and not understanding what all the fuss was about. The second book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5094.The_Drawing_of_the_Three__The_Dark_Tower___2_' title='The Drawing of the Three (The Dark Tower, #2) by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Drawing of the Three</a>, was more impressive and more complicated and though I liked it (after a three year gap after the first book) I was still unsure as to h</span>
  <span id="freeText6716594619655867632" style="display:none">“April is the cruellest month”<br><br>Stephen King’s ambitious and challenging Dark Tower series continues with the third novel, The Waste Lands, first published in 1991.<br><br>I am reading this series very slowly. I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43615.The_Gunslinger__The_Dark_Tower___1_" title="The Gunslinger (The Dark Tower, #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gunslinger</a> in 2012, not really sure what I had read and why and not understanding what all the fuss was about. The second book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5094.The_Drawing_of_the_Three__The_Dark_Tower___2_" title="The Drawing of the Three (The Dark Tower, #2) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Drawing of the Three</a>, was more impressive and more complicated and though I liked it (after a three year gap after the first book) I was still unsure as to how to contemplate and follow the storytelling.<br><br>“What are the roots that clutch, what branches grow<br>Out of this stony rubbish? Son of man,<br>You cannot say, or guess, for you know only<br>A heap of broken images, where the sun beats,<br>And the dead tree gives no shelter, the cricket no relief,<br>And the dry stone no sound of water.”<br><br>Now, I THINK I get it and am captivated. This is not just the Great American fantasy but the “world that has moved on “ is THE postmodern fantasy, rich with allusions to literature, film, art, and popular culture. The Gunslinger provided a foundation of medieval / feudal setting but with American western motifs and styles. In Roland of Gilead (who looks like Clint Eastwood) King has given us an impressionistic look into our world peripherally, seen in allegory in a world pulled free of it’s moorings – it has moved on. This is a world made up of not just the remains of our physical world, but also composed of the intellectual and cultural elements that form our perceptions and make us who we are.<br><br>“Here is the man with three staves, and here the Wheel,<br>And here is the one-eyed merchant, and this card,<br>Which is blank, is something he carries on his back,<br>Which I am forbidden to see. I do not find<br>The Hanged Man. Fear death by water.<br>I see crowds of people, walking round in a ring.<br>Thank you. If you see dear Mrs. Equitone,<br>Tell her I bring the horoscope myself:<br>One must be so careful these days.”<br><br>A casual reader, as I was initially, may be flustered by the surreal and even absurdist qualities of the writing, but King is not just imitating Beckett or Ionesco for absurdist sake, but rather to give life and breadth to a poetic attribution. The references to Browning and Elliot and all the other Easter eggs of reference and allusion are the detail with which King fills his landscape and discovering these hidden gems was part of the great fun of reading. ** I especially liked that King makes a Discworld reference with the turtle guardian with the world on its back.<br><br>“Unreal City<br>Under the brown fog of a winter noon<br>Mr. Eugenides, the Smyrna merchant<br>Unshaven, with a pocket full of currants<br>C.i.f. London: documents at sight,<br>Asked me in demotic French<br>To luncheon at the Cannon Street Hotel<br>Followed by a weekend at the Metropole.”<br><br>The inclusion of the city of Lud and of the train is a further connection to our world, but made strange and alien by King’s narrative. Likewise, the perspective from Roland shifts to Susannah and Eddie and Jake as their POV provides a scaled viewpoint from which to compare our world to King’s great vision. I love that King broke the fourth wall by discussing Jake’s essay about Roland and the Dark Tower and it is this kind of personality that gives this work life and makes it such an enjoyable, page turning book.<br><br>“In this decayed hole among the mountains<br>In the faint moonlight, the grass is singing<br>Over the tumbled graves, about the chapel<br>There is the empty chapel, only the wind’s home.<br>It has no windows, and the door swings,<br>Dry bones can harm no one.”<br><br>A great book and series and I am now fully on board. Highly recommended but you have to reads in order.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534337021i/26133242._SY540_.jpg" width="334" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="6716594619655867632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1004372153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1004372153" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1004372153?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444723465" href="/book/show/13083038-the-waste-lands">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=hanging-out-with-mrs-kholin">hanging-out-with-mrs-kholin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=the-dark-tower">the-dark-tower</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1004372153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1616442037307814821"><b>
  <i>"Behold ye, the return of the White! After evil ways and evil days, the White comes again! Be of good heart and hold up your heads, for ye have lived to see the wheel of ka begin to turn once more!"</i>
</b><br/><br/>What a journey! From incomprehensibly horrible to absodamnlutely fantastic to okay.<br/><br/>This book was all over the place. Both literally and metaphorically.<br/><br/>The first half is more of what we’re given in <i>The Drawing of the Three</i>. That is... a painfully boring story about Roland leaving his wildly interes</span>
  <span id="freeText1616442037307814821" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Behold ye, the return of the White! After evil ways and evil days, the White comes again! Be of good heart and hold up your heads, for ye have lived to see the wheel of ka begin to turn once more!"</i>
</b><br><br>What a journey! From incomprehensibly horrible to absodamnlutely fantastic to okay.<br><br>This book was all over the place. Both literally and metaphorically.<br><br>The first half is more of what we’re given in <i>The Drawing of the Three</i>. That is... a painfully boring story about Roland leaving his wildly interesting world behind to pick up three annoying travelling companions from different times and places in the city of New York.<br><br>To clarify for those still in doubt, I <s>fucking hated that shit</s> was slightly disappointed by these developments.<br><br>About halfway through however, the story steps into a whole new world (literally), and that world is like heaven compared to what has happened so far (to be frank, it wasn’t <i>that</i> good, but hey, after one and a half book of utter boredom you take what you can get).<br><br>Roland of Gilead assembles his company of gunslingers, and as the quest for the Dark Tower begins in earnest, the ka-tet arrives at the little town of River Crossing.<br><br><i>A great civil war - perhaps in Garlan, perhaps in a more distant land called Porla - had erupted three, perhaps even four hundred years ago. Its ripples had spread slowly outward, pushing anarchy and dissension ahead of them. Few if any kingdoms had been able to stand against those slow waves, and anarchy had come to this part of the world as surely as night follows sunset. At one time, whole armies had been on the roads, sometimes in advance, sometimes in retreat, always confused and without long-term goals. As time passed, they crumbled into smaller groups, and these degenerated into roving bands of harriers. Trade faltered, then broke down entirely. Travel went from a matter of inconvenience to one of danger. In the end, it became almost impossible. Communication with the city thinned steadily and had all but ceased a hundred and twenty years ago.<br><br>Like a hundred other towns Roland had ridden through - first with Cuthbert and the other gunslingers cast out of Gilead, then alone, in pursuit of the man in black - River Crossing had been cut off and thrown on its own resources.</i><br><br>River Crossing is a paradise of fantasy worldbuilding. While Stephen King has kept his cards close about the gunslingers and their world so far, he now starts showing his hand. And if you think this guy cannot really write fantasy, you are sorely mistaken.<br><br>Here starts a rain of epic stories and descriptions of places and names beyond any normal imagination...<br><br><i>“What is Mid-World?” Eddie asked.<br><br>“One of the large kingdoms which dominated the earth in the times before these. A kingdom of hope and knowledge and light—the sort of things we were trying to hold on to in my land before the darkness overtook us, as well. Some day if there’s time, I’ll tell you all the old stories . . . the ones I know, at least. They form a large tapestry, one which is beautiful but very sad.<br><br>“According to the old tales, a great city once stood at the edge of Mid-World - perhaps as great as your city of New York. It will be in ruins now, if it still exists at all. But there may be people... or monsters... or both. We’ll have to be on our guard."</i><br><br>The rest of the book is not quite as good as the amazing part at River Crossing, but it’s still much better than anything in the series since the opening sentence of the first book. However, it ends with a horrible cliffhanger. Well, not even a cliffhanger, but in the middle of a scene. It’s like one of those old TV shows ending with “To be continued” just at the climax.<br><br>But despite my ratings and sometimes low opinions, and even though it feels like the story hasn’t even started yet (three books in!), I’m greatly looking forward to the continuation.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447442194i/17005890._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><i>Dark Tower reviews</i>:</b><br>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/985852235" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Gunslinger</i>
</a><br>#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1004372145" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Drawing of the Three</i>
</a><br>#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1004372153" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Waste Lands</i>
</a><br>#4 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1004372161" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Wizard and Glass</i>
</a><br>#5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1423711681" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Wolves of the Calla</i>
</a><br>#6 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1423711775" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Song of Susannah</i>
</a><br>#7 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1423711845" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Dark Tower</i>
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1616442037307814821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2189536524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2189536524" />
    <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse"><img alt="Ms. Smartarse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401273675p2/13703358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2189536524?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms. Smartarse" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse">Ms. Smartarse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=oldies-but-goldies">oldies-but-goldies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=part_of_a_series">part_of_a_series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2189536524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17618305615544604569">The first two books painted an incredibly bleak picture of Roland's world. Said to have "<em>moved on</em>", just teeming with monsters, demons and the occasional unexpected horrifying incident. <br/><br/>As a passive observer, I could definitely see merit in learning more about it, but the highlight of each episode was by far the possibility of leaving it behind for the relative 'familiarity' of New York. Granted, I've only seen pictures of the city, but compared to the horror of fighting and eating lobstrosities</span>
  <span id="freeText17618305615544604569" style="display:none">The first two books painted an incredibly bleak picture of Roland's world. Said to have "<em>moved on</em>", just teeming with monsters, demons and the occasional unexpected horrifying incident. <br><br>As a passive observer, I could definitely see merit in learning more about it, but the highlight of each episode was by far the possibility of leaving it behind for the relative 'familiarity' of New York. Granted, I've only seen pictures of the city, but compared to the horror of fighting and eating lobstrosities on a daily basis, it at least <em>felt</em> safer.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525888366i/25512534._SX540_.jpg" alt="NYC in the 70s" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The third book however, brought on a subtle change in atmosphere, but it was enough to get me more interested in the post-apocalyptic world. I can't say I'm normally very keen on being mauled to death by giant bears, nor look forward to getting glimpses of crazy sick people, or the odd vivid monster feast or two. As long as I was reading however, the world of our heroes certainly <em>seemed</em> riveting enough.<br><br>The billy-bumbler just stole the show for me: totally adorable, occasionally heart-breaking (I even shed a tear of two during the bridge crossing scene), it managed to put me in an all-around good mood.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525888366i/25512533._SX540_.jpg" alt="bridge to Lud" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For all the excitement that I felt, compared to the previous two books, I couldn't honestly say that this one has held me completely spell-bound. I certainly liked to <em>read it</em>, and I definitely felt extremely excited about <em>picking it up</em>, however I didn't exactly dream about it while waiting for the chance to pick it up again.<br><br>Some passages were rather difficult to follow: such as the elders' stories about <em>old Lud</em>. Probably due to my unfamiliarity with the language of this world, not to mention the weirdly fragmented manner people told things.<br><br><strong>Score: 4/5 stars</strong><br><br>Stephen put it best in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30377238" rel="nofollow noopener">his review</a>: the "<em>Shardik-Lud Expedition</em>".<br><br>Not sure if it's mostly due to the improved writing style, or even just the cliff-hanger ending, but I'm definitely looking forward to the next book.<br><br>========================<br>Review of book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2053296648" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gunslinger</a><br>Review of book 2:<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2060681141" rel="nofollow noopener">The Drawing of the Three</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17618305615544604569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1527433438" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1527433438" />
    <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan"><img alt="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101944p2/4728718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1527433438?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan">Algernon (Darth Anyan)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/94767.The_Waste_Lands">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1527433438" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13127075675637156045"><br/><b> Some day if there’s time, I’ll tell you all the old stories ... the ones I know, at least. They form a large tapestry, one which is beautiful but very sad. </b><br/><br/>Some fine day ... but not today and not in this third installment of the Dark Tower series. For now, Roland and his friends are too busy doing nothing much for about six hundred pages. They travel, they fight the ocassional monster or deranged mob leader, the sit by the campfire and have some obscure nightmares and prophetic visions. All wra</span>
  <span id="freeText13127075675637156045" style="display:none"><br /><b> Some day if there’s time, I’ll tell you all the old stories ... the ones I know, at least. They form a large tapestry, one which is beautiful but very sad. </b><br /><br />Some fine day ... but not today and not in this third installment of the Dark Tower series. For now, Roland and his friends are too busy doing nothing much for about six hundred pages. They travel, they fight the ocassional monster or deranged mob leader, the sit by the campfire and have some obscure nightmares and prophetic visions. All wrapped up in a hefty dose of mysticism, predestination and ambiguity.<br /><br /><i> For every thing I do know, there are a hundred things I don’t. You – both of you – will have to reconcile yourselves to that fact. The world has moved on, we say. When it did, it went like a great receding wave, leaving only wreckage behind ... wreckage that sometimes looks like a map. </i><br /><br />It looks to me more like the author is winging it, improvising the story as he swears that it will make sense in the end, once he finds out how to deliver on his promises of epicness. <br /><br />My criticism should be taken with a ‘reader advisory’ as a very subjective reaction, since most of my friends here rate this third novel, and the series in general as one of the best things that ever happened to speculative fiction. Personally I am bored, and only my obsesive compulsion to finish whatever I start is keeping me going. I was reading about the gunslinger’s journey across the waste lands in parallel with the revenge melodrama of Edmont Dantes, and almost every evening I would pick Dumas over King. I also finished the Dumas a good two weeks before the King, despite the former having almost double the page count.<br /><br />Your mileage might vary, and other readers will prefer allusions and delayed gratification over explicit plot and worldbuilding. For me, as I remarked right from the opening volume, The Dark Tower remains a triumph of style over substance: an exceedingly well written story that aims to create a mood rather than to present an epic adventure. The adventure and the worldbuilding are present, undoubtedly, but they are drip-fed to the reader in between long passages of walking and wondering what the heck is going on. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ in this book the set pieces are : a fight with a giant bear, a dramatic crossing of a portal between worlds by Jake, the crossing of a high suspension bridge, an undergound duel in a dying city. All good and spectacular, but do they justify the length of the novel?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Stephen King forte so far in this series is his ability to capture anxiety and fear in his characters. The interplay between the members of the ‘ka-tet’ is also helping to turn the pages, but I believe the author is at his best when he tries to scare the reader:<br /><br /><i> From solid ground, the bridge seemed to be swaying only a little, but once he was actually on it, he felt as if he were standing on the pendulum of the world’s biggest grandfather clock. The movement was very slow, but it was regular, and the length of the swings was much longer than he had anticipated. </i><br /><br />Hit and miss are the pop culture references that are more prominent here than in the previous two episodes, and a half-hearted attempt to unite the two best settings of King : “The Dark Tower” and “The Stand”. Let me try to illustrate my points:<br /><br />-	I am a big fan of Richard Adams, and “Shardik” was one of the first novels I read as an adult that brought me back to fantasy. One version of Shardik is roaming the waste lands, and if I were in the mood for speculation, I could probably draw some parallels with the death of myths in both fictional universes. I am also a big fan of Z Z Top, and I was thrilled to find one of their songs featured here. Both references though failed to be an integral part of King’s story and feel more like a nod and a wink to the fans right now instead of a true key to unlock the mysteries of the gunslinger world. Other similar nods and winks are directed at Asimov (positronics), Shirley Jackson (The Loterry), a children’s book about trains that I am not familiar with, Greek mythology (The Sphinx) and Harlan Ellison (The TickTockMan). They may all be part of the project to anchor the imaginary world to the real, historical Earth that Roland &amp; Co. can visit through the warp-gates but, like the backstory of the gunslinger, the connection is left for a later episode.<br /><br />-	There is a significant moment in the middle of the book that shows Roland in a new light (and thus might be considered a spoiler!1!), a sequence that made me think immediately of The Stand : <br /><br /><i> When they reached Roland, they knelt before him and touched the sandalwood butt of the revolver which jutted from the holster he wore on his left hip. He put his hands on their shoulders and kissed their old brows. </i><br /><br />Will the whole epic quest to discover the Dark Tower be reduced to a battle between the forces of Good and Evil, with two god-like creatures leading the opposing armies? Roland seems destined to be the avatar of Good, and later on there is even a gigantic statue of him in the manner of the Colossus of Rhodes. And (more spoilers !!!) of course he is chased by a creature of darkness :<br /><br /><i> “I’m a man of many handles, pardner,” the man said from inside the darkness of his hood, and although his voice was grave, Tick-Tock heard laughter lurking just below the surface. “There’s some that call me Jimmy, and some that call me Timmy; some that call me Handy and some that call me Dandy. They can call me Loser, or they can call me Winner, just as long as they don’t call me in too late for dinner.” </i><br /><br />I will probably read the next book in the series while I still remember what went on in this one, but right now I don’t consider it a priority, and I can only echo one of Roland’s exasperated companions, baffled by the nature of the waste lands and the secretive atitude of the gunslinger :<br /><br /><b> “When are you going to tell us what you do know?” Eddie asked the next morning. </b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13127075675637156045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1240516714" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1240516714" />
    <a title="Stepheny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny"><img alt="Stepheny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567725280p2/7091879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1240516714?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stepheny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stepheny" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny">Stepheny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780452267404" href="/book/show/995127.The_Waste_Lands">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=all-hail-the-crimson-king">all-hail-the-crimson-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=dystopians">dystopians</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=badd-ass-fantasy">badd-ass-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=like-a-meth-addiction">like-a-meth-addiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=guilty-pleasure-reads">guilty-pleasure-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=hands-down-favorites">hands-down-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1240516714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer505619638676563054"><br/><br/>4.5 stars<br/><br/><b> The Waste Lands</b> is the third installment in the Dark Tower series. I’ve been through this series so many times over the years I have lost count. But what has made this trip so important is all of the wonderful people I have gotten to take along the Path of the Beam. I would like to thank my posse for allowing me to hold their hands and guide them on this most epic of quests. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1241105245' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rootin’ Tootin Pistol Packin’ Delee</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1126524438' rel='nofollow noopener'> Jumpin’ Jeff</a> , <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1036857718' rel='nofollow noopener'> Calamity Bev</a> and last but certainly not least, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/840710676' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bronco Bust</a></span>
  <span id="freeText505619638676563054" style="display:none"><br /><br />4.5 stars<br /><br /><b> The Waste Lands</b> is the third installment in the Dark Tower series. I’ve been through this series so many times over the years I have lost count. But what has made this trip so important is all of the wonderful people I have gotten to take along the Path of the Beam. I would like to thank my posse for allowing me to hold their hands and guide them on this most epic of quests. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1241105245" rel="nofollow noopener">Rootin’ Tootin Pistol Packin’ Delee</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1126524438" rel="nofollow noopener"> Jumpin’ Jeff</a> , <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1036857718" rel="nofollow noopener"> Calamity Bev</a> and last but certainly not least, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/840710676" rel="nofollow noopener">Bronco Bustin’ Black Jackin’ Jason</a><br /><br /> I am a pusher of books, anyone who has had even a minute’s interaction with me can attest to this. I get especially pushy when I know the books could change someone’s life. There is only a handful of books that fall into that category for me-obviously, the Harry Potter series and of course, the Dark Tower series.<br /><br />While I love the shit out of Harry Potter, the Dark Tower series actually changed my view on life and what it all means. I had a breakthrough. I’ve always been a cynical, show me don’t tell me type and the Dark Tower series gave me something to believe in; something that made sense to me. I’ve never been religious, but I’m not an Atheist either. I fall more in line with Agnostics. My problem is that I want to believe everything so much I can’t believe anything.<br /><br />Ka. <br /><br />Ka is something all of its own. It does not bend to your will. It does not care for your plans. If you detour around it, you’ll still find yourself where you were meant to be. The wheel of Ka keeps turning and your best bet is to sit back and enjoy the ride. There’s truly no point in fighting it. <br /><br />We start out with one hell of a paradox. Poor Roland, given the events in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1180967074?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener"> the Drawing of the Three</a> is torn between what happened and what didn’t happen. Did Jake accompany him through the desert and up the mountains? Did Jake exist in this world? Did Roland let him fall? How could he have let him fall if he was never there? Roland is in rough shape and only the key can help.<br /><br />Eddie and Susannah have taken nuptial vows and found a love that is both deserving and beautiful. They are a good match for one another, though, if I am to be honest, I think <b>I</b> would be a much better match for Eddie. Maybe the wheel of Ka will roll through and make that happen for me? What do you say, Ka?! <br /><br />*looks around hopefully*<br /><br />Eddie sees that he will need to play a big role in Jake’s drawing into this world. What he doesn’t know is if he is cut out for it, or if he’ll be ready in time. Eddie is constantly at war with himself from the years of being mentally beat down by his older brother. <br /><br />Susannah Dean, who was once Odetta Holmes and Detta Walker, is trying her best to maintain her one mind now that her alternate personalities have been forced to face one another. She is also trying to figure out her place in this new strange place.<br /><br />Jake’s drawing into this world is by far my favorite sequence in this whole book. It is such an intense turn of events. The splitting minds, the split perspective and most especially the fact that while Eddie’s door faces down, Jake enters it vertically just creates this insane imagry that blows me away every time.<br /><br />Then there is Oy. What a wonderful creature King has produced. Oy makes my heart feel so happy with love and pride I can hardly contain myself. He represents all that is good and innocent in this world and his relationship with ‘Ake is one of the best parts of the Dark Tower series.<br /><br />Our favorite Ka-Tet is on the Path of the Beam in search of Blaine the Mono. Blain is a pain, and this they know; but he is also a necessity to their quest. Will they make it to him in time? Will Blaine still be there? If he is there, is he sane? Can a train <i>be</i> sane? Where will this story go?<br /><br />The Waste Lands, while not as good as Drawing of the Three, gives us insight into some of King’s best written characters. We get to know them individually while seeing them interact with one another. My favorite interactions are between Roland and Eddie. Roland, so severe and earnest in every aspect vs. the nonstop joker, Eddie, makes for some great entertainment. The character arcs throughout this series are some of the most fascinating that I’ve ever had the pleasure of reading. Each and every time I read this series I find something new that makes me love them all the more. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“[Eddie] cried out but his cry was lost in the golden blast of some tremendous horn. It came from the top of the Tower, and seemed to fill the world. As that note of warning held and drew out over the field where he stood, blackness welled from the windows which girdled the Tower. It overspilled them and spread across the sky in flaggy streams which came together and formed a growing blotch of darkness. It did not look like a cloud; it looked like a tumor hanging over the earth. The sky was blotted out. And, he saw, it was not a cloud or a tumor but a shape, some tenebrous, cyclopean shape racing toward the place where he stood.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="505619638676563054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13537691458567722039">As usual I have nothing but positive things to say about this book. Well, actually there is one negative and that's the ending. It was of course an incomplete work ending at a climax, however, since it's not 1991 anymore and I do not have to wait years for a new book to come out, I will not fault King for this. In fact, I will look at it as a positive, for I cannot wait to begin book 4. <br/><br/>Mid-world is continuing to grow, and the questions to its existence continue to be answered. It's funny, while</span>
  <span id="freeText13537691458567722039" style="display:none">As usual I have nothing but positive things to say about this book. Well, actually there is one negative and that's the ending. It was of course an incomplete work ending at a climax, however, since it's not 1991 anymore and I do not have to wait years for a new book to come out, I will not fault King for this. In fact, I will look at it as a positive, for I cannot wait to begin book 4. <br /><br />Mid-world is continuing to grow, and the questions to its existence continue to be answered. It's funny, while reading this you cannot believe how brilliant King's mind is to have the kind of foresight he did in creating this fantasy only to find out he's the first to admit the story wrote itself. <br /><br />I'm excited to continue the adventure of Roland and his Ka-tet, and see how they survive Blaine the Mono's challenge. </span>

<div id="review_966025594" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/966025594" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/966025594?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
