        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/94767.The_Waste_Lands">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=western">western</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=will-read-again">will-read-again</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer966025594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14696698465373528628">The thing with this series is that it just gets better along the way. <br/><br/>This review might contain some spoilers? I'm not sure if some people would consider them as spoilers, so read at your own risk! You've been warned.<br/><br/>The most amazing thing about this book would be the fact that Jake fucking Chambers is back! If you've read my review of The Gunslinger (book 1) then you'd know how much I love that kid. We can be friends again King, that much I can say. <br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Fuck you, Roland. You let him</span></span>
  <span id="freeText14696698465373528628" style="display:none">The thing with this series is that it just gets better along the way. <br /><br />This review might contain some spoilers? I'm not sure if some people would consider them as spoilers, so read at your own risk! You've been warned.<br /><br />The most amazing thing about this book would be the fact that Jake fucking Chambers is back! If you've read my review of The Gunslinger (book 1) then you'd know how much I love that kid. We can be friends again King, that much I can say. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Fuck you, Roland. You let him go again. You promised you wouldn't. Even though you saved him in the end, you're still one mother fucking asshole who should burn in hell. I still like you as a character though, but fuck you nonetheless.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This novel revolved around the first half of Roland and his crew's quest for The Dark Tower. King delivered what he promised. It was an eventful and amazing first half. A lot of struggles along the way, and a lot of riddles too. And a huge amount of heart racing scenes. This is another great example of a page turner. Aside from the main quest though, the story ventured out into Jake's life in New York. It only took a few chapters of the whole book, but those few chapters were really great for me. Not only did King further developed Jake's character, but he also made him even more likable. <br /><br />Aside from Jake though, the crew also developed quite well in this third installment. Eddie was his usual funny self, but Susannah was still a bit boring for me. I just don't see her as a character that I'd like a lot, but we'll see in the long run. Oy the dog was just as amazing as Jake, or so I believe he's a dog. I like animals in books, so Oy just made it to my favorites list.<br /><br />King wrote one hell of a cliffhanger. Aside from the cliffhanger, I heard that the next book concentrates on something else. If he doesn't continue the story, I might be a little pissed off. I'm just glad that the series is complete already though, and I don't have to wait for the next ones to come out. I've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6595548?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Kemper's review</a> and yeah, I'm glad I can binge read this series.<br /><br />5/5 stars. Can't wait to know what's going to happen next. This series is really starting to become my favorite series of all time.</span>

<div id="review_2062838492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2062838492" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2062838492?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2062838492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10568744071749376718"><i>“Ka—the word you think of as ‘destiny,’ Eddie, although the actual meaning is much more complex and hard to define, as is almost always the case with words of the High Speech. And tet, which means a group of people with the same interests and goals. We three are a tet, for instance. Ka-tet is the place where many lives are joined by fate.”</i><br/><br/>This is the book where Roland’s <i>ka-tet</i> is fully formed*, with the addition of eleven years old Jake Chambers and Oy the billy-bumbler (a Mid-World species). <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500276041i/23316492._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Ka</span>
  <span id="freeText10568744071749376718" style="display:none"><i>“Ka—the word you think of as ‘destiny,’ Eddie, although the actual meaning is much more complex and hard to define, as is almost always the case with words of the High Speech. And tet, which means a group of people with the same interests and goals. We three are a tet, for instance. Ka-tet is the place where many lives are joined by fate.”</i><br><br>This is the book where Roland’s <i>ka-tet</i> is fully formed*, with the addition of eleven years old Jake Chambers and Oy the billy-bumbler (a Mid-World species). <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500276041i/23316492._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ka-Tet. Art by <a href="http://www.michaelwhelan.com/galleries/dark-tower-ka-tet/" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael Whelan</a><br><br>In this eventful installment Roland, Eddie and Susannah continue their quest for the Dark Tower, along the way Roland starts going insane as his recent timeline has been doubled due to an incident in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10366941.The_Dark_Tower_II_The_Drawing_of_the_Three_by_Stephen_King___Summary___Study_Guide" title="The Dark Tower II The Drawing of the Three by Stephen King - Summary &amp; Study Guide by BookRags" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Dark Tower II: The Drawing of the Three</a> in which Jake Chambers who died in book #1 is saved through Roland interfering with a key event in his past. This causes a paradox where both Roland and Jake remember two alternate versions of the past, and the conflicting versions fight for supremacy in their minds. To save Roland’s sanity, Roland, Eddie and Susannah must help Jake to cross over from our Earth into Mid-World, an extremely dangerous task involving entry into a nasty magic circle in Mid-World, guarded by a sex-crazed demon, on Jake’s side (in our world) the portal is in a haunted house with a monstrous gatekeeper. This mission forms the first half of <i>The Waste Lands</i>, it makes for a hair-raising adventure with a very dark undertone, as depicted on the cover of this hardback edition:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500276041i/23316494.jpg" width="300" height="441" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Don’t worry, I won’t give you much info on what transpires in the equally hectic second half of the book, but it does involve a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32198259-charlie-the-choo-choo" rel="nofollow noopener">crazy train</a> (nothing to do with Ozzy).<br><br>I am tremendously enjoying this Dark Tower series reread; this is the only advantageous aspect of having a memory like a sieve, I can enjoy these books just as much as the first time I read them. Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5094.The_Drawing_of_the_Three__The_Dark_Tower___2_" title="The Drawing of the Three (The Dark Tower, #2) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Drawing of the Three</a> <i>The Waste Lands</i> is packed with incident and characterization engrossing (the first book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43615.The_Gunslinger__The_Dark_Tower___1_" title="The Gunslinger (The Dark Tower, #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Gunslinger</a> is very good but less intense). Interestingly there is more of a sci-fi element in this installment with mad AIs, cyborgs (also mad), high technology, and computers; lest we forget, this is a world where magic and technology coexist. It is also very nice to find tributes to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov" title="Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener"> Isaac Asimov</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7717.Richard_Adams" title="Richard Adams" rel="nofollow noopener"> Richard Adams</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/656983.J_R_R__Tolkien" title="J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener"> J. R. R. Tolkien</a> in the narrative; it is like finding that your favorite band also dig your other favorite bands. King puts a lot of effort into developing his characters, this has always been his secret weapon. However, what makes the Dark Tower series stand out among thousands of other fantasy series is the western aesthetic of Mid-World, and also Roland’s forays into our world and. This makes a nice change to the standard medieval setting of most epic fantasy series; the sci-fi and horror aspects further distinguishes it from the others.<br><br>Unlike the previous two volumes <i>The Waste Lands</i> ends on a cliff hanger, as the entire series is completed this should not be a cause for concern. I imagine most people who have read the previous books are bound to want to read this one. When you have come this far the rest is unavoidable. <br>Should you read this book? In the end, all things, even this review, serve the Dark Tower.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500276041i/23316495.jpg" alt="roses line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Notes</b><br>* Another character is added to the ka-tet in book #5, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4978.Wolves_of_the_Calla__The_Dark_Tower___5_" title="Wolves of the Calla (The Dark Tower, #5) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener"> Wolves of the Calla</a>. but these five are the classic lineup.<br><br>• An excellent companion to this book is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32198259.Charlie_the_Choo_Choo_From_the_world_of_The_Dark_Tower" title="Charlie the Choo-Choo From the world of The Dark Tower by Beryl Evans" rel="nofollow noopener"> Charlie the Choo-Choo: From the world of The Dark Tower</a>, a creepy faux-children’s book. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500276041i/23316493._SX540_.jpg" width="350" height="327" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>• Guns and roses play an important part in this book, nothing to do with Axl Rose.<br><br>• The song “<a href="https://youtu.be/F89McWFENTs" rel="nofollow noopener"> Velcro Fly </a>” is also significant in this book, it has everything to do with ZZ Top.<br><br>• Wild West themed fantasy is not unique to the Dark Tower series, it is a subgenre called “weird west”. If you are interested there is a list of these books on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weird_West" rel="nofollow noopener">this Wikipedia page</a>. I have not read any of the books listed there (apart from Dark Tower, obviously) but I have read another excellent “weird west” series. It is called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/53254-jon-shannow" rel="nofollow noopener"> Jon Shannow Series</a> by the wonderful and much missed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11586.David_Gemmell" title="David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener"> David Gemmell</a>. If you have read all the Dark Towers I recommend checking it out, Gemmell is a very different author from Stephen King so you don’t need to worry if it will read like an imitation.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500276041i/23316495.jpg" alt="roses line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Quotes:</b><br><i>“There were a lot of stories for kids with stuff like this in them, stuff that threw acid all over your emotions. Hansel and Gretel being turned out into the forest, Bambi’s mother getting scragged by a hunter, the death of Old Yeller. It was easy to hurt little kids, easy to make them cry, and this seemed to bring out a strangely sadistic streak in many storytellers.”<br><br>“Whatever his head thought about this gunslinging business, his hands had discovered they liked it just fine.”<br><br>“We are ka-tet,” Roland began, “which means a group of people bound together by fate. The philosophers of my land said a ka-tet could only be broken by death or treachery.<br><br>“In the fierce furnace of Elmer Chambers’s mind, the gross carbon of wish and opinion was often blasted into the hard diamonds which he called facts . . . or, in more informal circumstances, “factoids.””<br><br>“He called it The Net of Eratosthenes. Take me over to dat box on the wall, Roland—I’m goan answer dat honkey computer’s riddle. I’m goan th’ow you a net and catch you a train-ride.”</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500279004i/23316900._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Oy the Billy-Bumbler <a href="http://www.deviantart.com/art/Oy-the-Billy-Bumbler-670664066" rel="nofollow noopener">by kenket</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10568744071749376718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

(I forgot how much I loved Oy and his golden eyes!) Even some of my old enemies are here, Gasher and Blane the Mono. <br/><br/>It's nice re-reading these via audio, even if I have to wait a few weeks in between books while waiting for the next audio book to come in to the library.   <span id="freeText4867758333401487977" style="display:none">Even though I'm not crazy about this narrator, Frank Muller, I ended up giving my audio re-read of this book an extra star.<br /><br />All my old friends are together again: Roland, Susannah, Eddie, Jack and even Oy. (I forgot how much I loved Oy and his golden eyes!) Even some of my old enemies are here, Gasher and Blane the Mono. <br /><br />It's nice re-reading these via audio, even if I have to wait a few weeks in between books while waiting for the next audio book to come in to the library. This time I don't have to wait years in between books which keeps everything fresh in my mind. <br /><br />I have to respect a mind that is so wildly imaginative that it can put together a story of this scope. It blows me away. I guess that's why Stephen is the King. At least in my book. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5782678631393640727">3.5 stars and I was frustrated enough with this volume in the continuing saga NOT to round up to 4. Steven King has a reputation for waffling, but this is the first time in the Dark Tower series, where I really felt the reader suffered because of it. I loved Oy the Bumbler. <br/>Had I not been listening to this rather than simply reading it, I am not at all sure I would have finished it.<br/>I consider myself very lucky not to have to wait the many years between the writing of this novel and the next in t</span>
  <span id="freeText5782678631393640727" style="display:none">3.5 stars and I was frustrated enough with this volume in the continuing saga NOT to round up to 4. Steven King has a reputation for waffling, but this is the first time in the Dark Tower series, where I really felt the reader suffered because of it. I loved Oy the Bumbler. <br />Had I not been listening to this rather than simply reading it, I am not at all sure I would have finished it.<br />I consider myself very lucky not to have to wait the many years between the writing of this novel and the next in the series; nevertheless, I won't be reading book 4 quite as quickly as I might have; this is still a wonderful series but my enthusiasm has been dimmed by the slow pacing and drawing out of events. I have also gleaned from reviews that book 4 is itself pretty slow.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9389316070054905090">I loved this book. I love the connections between the characters' past lives and between Mid-World and Our When. I also felt a strong link to other Stephen King books: a mansion in Brooklyn comes to life and it was The Overlook all over again for me. The middle of the book (the mansion part) was the most amazing part of a completely amazing story. It could have just ended there for me emotionally, but it's all about the quest. So, onward to Lud which brings every nuked out NYC full of mutants an</span>
  <span id="freeText9389316070054905090" style="display:none">I loved this book. I love the connections between the characters' past lives and between Mid-World and Our When. I also felt a strong link to other Stephen King books: a mansion in Brooklyn comes to life and it was The Overlook all over again for me. The middle of the book (the mansion part) was the most amazing part of a completely amazing story. It could have just ended there for me emotionally, but it's all about the quest. So, onward to Lud which brings every nuked out NYC full of mutants and psychos immediately to mind. Also amazing, exciting and full of connections. <br /><br />S.K. foreshadowed a lot of character and plot development in this book, so thank goodness I don't have to wait six years for Book 4. Next month: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5096.Wizard_and_Glass__The_Dark_Tower___4_" title="Wizard and Glass (The Dark Tower, #4) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Wizard and Glass</a>!<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18503031-the-waste-lands-dark-tower-3" rel="nofollow noopener">March 2017 Buddy Read</a></span>

<div id="review_570510629" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17032842563593982527">This volume of the Dark Tower has aged like fine wine, fascinating me more than all the previous volumes with the inclusion of more and more ancient tech. The breaking down of knowledge, society, and sanity is the main thrill, seeing the high-tech descendants of a massive, glorious metropolis that has Moved On act like ignorant yokels.<br/><br/>Lud. *sigh*<br/><br/>But my personal huge, roaring favorite has got to be Shardik. What a guardian! Glorious! And with a thinking cap on, too! :)<br/><br/>But when it comes to charact</span>
  <span id="freeText17032842563593982527" style="display:none">This volume of the Dark Tower has aged like fine wine, fascinating me more than all the previous volumes with the inclusion of more and more ancient tech. The breaking down of knowledge, society, and sanity is the main thrill, seeing the high-tech descendants of a massive, glorious metropolis that has Moved On act like ignorant yokels.<br /><br />Lud. *sigh*<br /><br />But my personal huge, roaring favorite has got to be Shardik. What a guardian! Glorious! And with a thinking cap on, too! :)<br /><br />But when it comes to characters, King has got almost everyone beat. The two Deans, Roland himself, and the inclusion of the much-missed Jake and their new little friend makes this Ka-Tet one that will forever live in my memory. As, indeed, it already has. This is my third read and I still love it.<br /><br />But my last shout-out has got to be for Blaine. Blaine's a pain. Indeed he is. Choo-Choo!!!<br /><br />The Dark Tower series is definitely one of the best fantasies ever written. None others have the sheer imagination or as much SCOPE. And to think that New York City can be a microcosm of the multiverse, showing us how As Above, So Below, all things can forever mirror each other? Brilliant. :)<br /><br />I would now like a rose, please. :)<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1357622550" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1357622550" />
    <a title="Ron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43881851-ron"><img alt="Ron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557265090p2/43881851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1357622550?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ron" href="/user/show/43881851-ron">Ron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1357622550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6303636952863421680"><i>
  <b>* spoilers spoilers spoilers *</b>
</i><br/><br/>It is both difficult and easy to say just why this book, The Waste Lands, is even better than The Drawing of the Three. That’s no small feat to accomplish because The Drawing of the Three is a terrific book. But when I first questioned why I liked this one a little more, I couldn't explain the why of it even to myself. With thought though it became clearer. First off, it's a roller coaster ride of a story (much like the second book actually - picking up only a f</span>
  <span id="freeText6303636952863421680" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>* spoilers spoilers spoilers *</b>
</i><br /><br />It is both difficult and easy to say just why this book, The Waste Lands, is even better than The Drawing of the Three. That’s no small feat to accomplish because The Drawing of the Three is a terrific book. But when I first questioned why I liked this one a little more, I couldn't explain the why of it even to myself. With thought though it became clearer. First off, it's a roller coaster ride of a story (much like the second book actually - picking up only a few months and a few miles from where it had left off) that starts at the top of the coaster slope with the arrival of Shardik. By the way, if that name sounds familiar to you, but you can't quite place it, King has a little fun with the hinting of it in the book too. Much like The Drawing of the Three gives the reader no time before the Lobstrocities arrive, this book does the same with this giant, angry bear. And what's good about this is not just the excitement, but the pieces of information about The Dark Tower, the Beams, and these Guardians we've suddenly stumbled upon. The answers also have a way of creating more questions, but for me, that's part of the ride. As our Ka-tet finds and follows this new path of the beam, the book has a sudden direction with a course that seems set. The problem is that something is missing from the group. Feelings about that missing piece are subtly hidden within the pages long before we realize Roland is in the middle of a breakdown, so that Jake is on our minds as much as he's on Roland's. This is where I wondered about my thoughts the first time around. Did I think then that Jake would return? I just can't remember. Did King know before writing it? He never plans ahead, but my guess is he did with this one thing. Jake is a cornerstone, and the way he's returned is brilliant. The only thing that could possibly make it better is the inclusion of one billy bumbler. But just as King plays with the fate of a character in the previous books, he does so again here. The tension comes back big time - only to be eclipsed by the cliffhanger ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6303636952863421680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3110914589?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3110914589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12330133529561138543">What a tease! This is one hell of a cliffhanger ending. *lol*<br/><br/>Susannah, Eddie and Roland continue their journey, but along the way it becomes clear that there is another member of their Ka-tet that still needs to join them and that it will be slightly more difficult to unite them with him. I'm talking about <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[the boy Jake <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br/>Actually, who that member was, was not really a surprise and therefore it's not really a spoiler. I really liked that King continued to spin the thr</span>
  <span id="freeText12330133529561138543" style="display:none">What a tease! This is one hell of a cliffhanger ending. *lol*<br /><br />Susannah, Eddie and Roland continue their journey, but along the way it becomes clear that there is another member of their Ka-tet that still needs to join them and that it will be slightly more difficult to unite them with him. I'm talking about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the boy Jake <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br />Actually, who that member was, was not really a surprise and therefore it's not really a spoiler. I really liked that King continued to spin the thread of the paradox introduced in the previous book <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when Roland entered the body of Jake's murderer and killed him before he could kill Jake <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br />It's HOW that member finds his way to the group, HOW they help him leave his NYC (slight time difference to Eddie's) and get him through a door to Midworld that is so interesting.<br />Just like what we keep seeing along the way until they get <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jake <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> through the door. In this case, it was really very fun to see the guardians such as Shardik (the bear) or the world turtle. It's an old myth that has been used by many authors before but I liked King's take on it that they are <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[pieces of technology <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> thousands of years old and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[breaking down <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> now that the world(s) has(have) moved on. Just like I loved getting a glimpse at that mega-city. Tragically interesting to see the decendants of a technological empire not really understanding their inheritance. So much misremembered or forgotten, the broken ruins lying around or slumbering underground. Sometimes even strewn across the landscape, broken and discarded. It's like a graveyard. <br />And then there was the train. Bwahahahahahaha! That was delightfully evil - and yes, I'll read the imaginary kid's book now as it will probably be immense fun!<br />Oh, and I loved <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jake's <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> dog-like friend! So cute!<br /><br />So we actually did cross a large area, moving purposefully in the right direction and meeting interesting (heartbreaking) people as well as creatures, structures and technology along the way. The worldbuilding here is insane! So rich, so deep ... more layers than an onion!<br /><br />I also didn't really have a problem with a certain scene I've been referring to in one of my status updates. I mean, this is about everything coming to a stop, a multiverse's fate hanging in the balance, everything being infested with desolation and death, your worst fears coming true. So it was only a matter of time until <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[rape <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> became a topic. However, as weird as King might have handled it, it was also an interesting (if slightly sinister) reversal. Detta for the win! *lol*<br />I'm seriously in love with the fact that King made one of his heroes not only a female and not only a black female but a black female who is a double amputee!<br /><br />We spend more time with the single characters, see them learn and grow (and I'm not only referring to their shooting skills), witness them becoming this tight-knit family, being about the only light in the ever-spreading darkness.<br /><br />Yep, I'm thoroughly hooked (as can be seen by the fact that I've read 4.5 books relating to this series in one month already - and I might keep going after only a short break of a few days). Especially since a certain someone has made a re-appearance (under a ridiculously obvious false name) and is drawing on strings once more - as was bound to happen.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer328408451949542307">5 Stars <br/><br/>Wow….. Well what a book! <br/><br/>This book definitely read as a fantasy more than a horror but it’s so magnificent! <br/><br/>The third series in the - The Dark Tower series and it’s a cracking book. I was a little gutted that I hadn’t read this series earlier as I am a HUGE Stephen king fan. Having said that I think that 24 is the perfect age to read this! I remember trying to read the Gunslinger as a pre-teen and it was just too confusing and too hard to read! Now at 24 I GET IT! <br/><br/>This series seems to be</span>
  <span id="freeText328408451949542307" style="display:none">5 Stars <br /><br />Wow….. Well what a book! <br /><br />This book definitely read as a fantasy more than a horror but it’s so magnificent! <br /><br />The third series in the - The Dark Tower series and it’s a cracking book. I was a little gutted that I hadn’t read this series earlier as I am a HUGE Stephen king fan. Having said that I think that 24 is the perfect age to read this! I remember trying to read the Gunslinger as a pre-teen and it was just too confusing and too hard to read! Now at 24 I GET IT! <br /><br />This series seems to be getting less and less confusing as it goes on. Stephen King really has created a whole world within these books and reading it developing is truly BEAUTIFUL I love this series! I can’t wait to move on to the next! <br /><br />As always Stephen King’s character building is next to none and by this book the reader is really getting deep into the characters minds and personality which isn’t easier with some of them! <br />Honestly a masterpiece I don’t know how King comes up with any of this but I bow to him! CHARLIE THE CHO-CHOOO! <br /><br />"Don't ask me silly questions, I won't play silly games, I'm just a simple choo choo train<br />And I'll always be the same. I only want to race along. Beneath the bright blue sky and be a happy choo choo train. Until the day I die."<br /><br />"The wheel of ka turns and the world moves on."<br /><br />"The gunslinger is the truth. Roland is the truth. The Prisoner is the truth. The Lady of Shadows is the truth. The Prisoner and the Lady are married. That is the truth. The way station is the truth. The Speaking Demon is the truth. We went under the mountains and that is the truth. There were monsters under the mountain. That is the truth. One of them had an Amoco gas pump between his legs and was pretending it was his penis. That is the truth. Roland let me die. That is the truth. I still love him. That is the truth."<br /><br />Jake is such a brilliant character too – such a switched on 11yr old and a real hero! He’s brave, strong, cleaver and BRILLIANT! The relationship between all the characters has really changed and grown and I am now fully invested into each of them! A REAL DREAM TEAM! <br /><br />The ending though….. I am so glad I already have the whole series ready to read if I had to wait for the forth to come out I would be gutted!<br /><br />On to the next! <br /></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3555535780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3555535780" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3555535780?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28335914-the-waste-lands">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=portal-fantasy">portal-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=western">western</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3555535780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11673571485332678340">And the award for creepiest train in all of literature goes to…<br/><blockquote>“Don't ask me silly questions<br/>I won't play silly games<br/>I'm just a simple choo choo train<br/>And I'll always be the same.<br/><br/>I only want to race along<br/>Beneath the bright blue sky<br/>And be a happy choo choo train<br/>Until the day I die.” </blockquote><br/>Stephen King has had a place among my favorite authors for 3 or 4 years now. <b>But over the span of this book and its predecessor, <i>The Drawing of the Three</i>, he’s edging remarkably close to becoming not just one of my favo</b></span>
  <span id="freeText11673571485332678340" style="display:none">And the award for creepiest train in all of literature goes to…<br /><blockquote>“Don't ask me silly questions<br />I won't play silly games<br />I'm just a simple choo choo train<br />And I'll always be the same.<br /><br />I only want to race along<br />Beneath the bright blue sky<br />And be a happy choo choo train<br />Until the day I die.” </blockquote><br />Stephen King has had a place among my favorite authors for 3 or 4 years now. <b>But over the span of this book and its predecessor, <i>The Drawing of the Three</i>, he’s edging remarkably close to becoming not just one of my favorite authors, but my hands down favorite.</b> Right now he’s in a three-way tie with Brandon Sanderson and Nora Roberts, but <i>Wizard and Glass </i>might actually change that if it holds a candle to <i>The Waste Lands</i>. I’ve heard that the back half of the Dark Tower series pales a bit in comparison to the first 4 books, so I’m trying to keep my expectations low, but <u>this is shaping up to be my favorite series of all time</u>.<br /><blockquote>“The wheel of ka turns and the world moves on.”</blockquote> <br /><i>The Gunslinger</i> was fine the first time I read it, and I enjoyed it more the second time around. I loved <i>The Drawing of the Three</i> almost immediately, and that love never wavered throughout the course of the novel. But <b><i>The Waste Lands</i> is one of my favorite books I’ve ever read.</b> <u>I’m not saying it’s one of the best books I’ve ever read</u>, as I’ve been fortunate enough to consume some absolute masterpieces. King’s prose doesn’t quite measure up to masterpiece quality. There are imperfections here. <b>But for sheer enjoyment value, for its ability to keep me so invested that I had a difficult time focussing on real life, for its insistence on invading my dreams even after I had read its final pages, this book just wins.</b> I was never less than completely entranced. The plot was astonishingly intricate and never lagged. I was never bored for a single second.<br /><blockquote>“See the turtle of enormous girth, on his shell he holds the earth. If you want to run and play, come along the beam today.”</blockquote><br /><u>I’m always amazed by the myriad of intricate ways in which King references his own work</u>. Some are small and incredibly subtle, while others are evident to even those who haven’t read a lot of his backlog. <b>And the self-referencing should seem haughty. It doesn’t. Instead, it makes everything King has ever written come across as purposeful and intentional and premeditative.</b> I have mad respect for this, and I think it makes his stellar stories even more enjoyable, as they build on one another. <u>I’m a huge lover of Easter eggs in stories</u>. It’s why I love Marvel and Sanderson’s Cosmere, and <b>it’s why I’ve come to adore King’s work.</b> And it’s exactly why I’ve chosen to take the much longer, circuitous route to the Tower. I’d love to just blast through the main series, but I’d love even more to pick up on as many of the little references to his other works that King has interwoven into the story as I possibly can. This will more than likely lead to me reading his entire body of work over the course of a decade or two, and I’m completely okay with that. <br /><blockquote>“In the end, all things, even the Beams, serve the Dark Tower. Did you think you would be any different?”</blockquote><br />The central cast of <i>The Waste Lands</i> completely won me over. <b>I love each member of this ka-tet with every fiber of my being.</b> And I can’t discuss a single one of them because, as with John Gwynne’s work, even mentioning certain character names could potentially spoil some important plot points. But also as with Gwynne’s work, I’m making an exception for an animal companion. <b>Oy the Billy-Bumbler is an absolute darling</b>, and I’m amazed at King’s ability to craft such a unique and lovable creature. <u>I need one.</u> Not want. NEED. I will say this about the central cast; they have all grown tremendously since each of them was introduced into the narrative. <b>There’s so much character development in this series that it’s unreal.</b> And their relationships with each other have experienced just as much transformation. It’s been truly wonderful to observe.<br /><blockquote>I do not aim with my hand. He who aims with his hand has forgotten the face of his father. I aim with my eye.<br />I do not shoot with my hand. He who shoots with his hand has forgotten the face of his father. I shoot with my mind.<br />I do not kill with my gun. He who kills with his gun has forgotten the face of his father. I kill with my heart.</blockquote><br />I have no idea where the wheel of Ka will take these companions. I would say that I can’t wait to find out, but I also know that King has no problem killing off his darlings and I’m terrified of what might lie ahead. But <b>the need to know is fierce, and I’m incredibly excited to continue my journey to the Tower.</b> And I can’t wait to see how more of King’s other works tie into it.<br /><br />Long days and pleasant nights, friends.<br /><br /><i>You can find <a href="https://wp.me/pa0WBY-2ro" rel="nofollow noopener"> this</a> review and more at <a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a>. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11673571485332678340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1874867674?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Daviau" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau">Ashley Daviau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781501161827" href="/book/show/30983471-the-waste-lands">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1874867674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15682553457143031803">I honestly think this might just be my favourite book out of this series. I say might because I must admit, my memory of the books that follow IS quite vague. So I might end up loving them even more than this one. <br/><br/>But I somehow doubt it because this magnificent book reintroduces one of my favourite characters from the series, introduces another favourite character AND introduces my favourite "villain" from this series. I won't name any names because I don't want to spoil it for anyone! <br/><br/>I also th</span>
  <span id="freeText15682553457143031803" style="display:none">I honestly think this might just be my favourite book out of this series. I say might because I must admit, my memory of the books that follow IS quite vague. So I might end up loving them even more than this one. <br /><br />But I somehow doubt it because this magnificent book reintroduces one of my favourite characters from the series, introduces another favourite character AND introduces my favourite "villain" from this series. I won't name any names because I don't want to spoil it for anyone! <br /><br />I also thoroughly enjoyed the world building that happened in this book, I feel like this is where King truly starts to hit his stride for this series! His writing is so beautifully detailed that I can see the landscape and the buildings emerging in my mind as I read and it is truly stunning! <br /><br />Despite this book being longer than both previous ones, it almost felt like it was shorter because it was just filled with so much action and development, it was hard to stop turning the pages once I picked it up! I was honestly on the edge of my seat so many times, I lost count and it's left me itching to revisit what happens next! </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('c725oISB6gfKgAvdQrcstNXPA0nahYGlie724ccayqY7rj56a2cybdojYHprlE6DoL6TMqU6lI3o+VgkFoQvCA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1OfQYu17OXQgTh++O5XfuUoqzZYI6KX6fmsXd9Nqkjyc9Fe4Ap3hHjDtdBkStr2OP1td7XdXsNIffLmyAvR3kg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
750,325
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7107439964949441579">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText7107439964949441579" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7107439964949441579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
